</li>
<li id="cite_note-27"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-27">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">He used <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> and German, knew enough <a href="/wiki/%E5%8F%A4%E5%B8%8C%E8%87%98%E8%AA%9E" title="古希腊语">Greek</a> to translate the 7th-century <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine" title="Byzantine">Byzantine</a> poet <span class="ilh-all" data-foreign-title="Theophylact Simocatta" data-lang-code="en" data-lang-name="英语" data-orig-title="Theophylact Simocatta"><span class="ilh-page"><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Theophylact_Simocatta&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Theophylact Simocatta（页面不存在）">Theophylact Simocatta</a></span><span class="noprint ilh-comment">（<span class="ilh-lang">英语</span><span class="ilh-colon">：</span><span class="ilh-link"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theophylact_Simocatta" title="en:Theophylact Simocatta"><span dir="auto" lang="en">Theophylact Simocatta</span></a></span>）</span></span>'s verses into Latin prose<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-armitage75–77_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-armitage75–77-24">[22]</a></sup> and "there is ample evidence that he knew the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Polish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Polish language（页面不存在）">Polish language</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davies26_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Davies26-25">[23]</a></sup> During his several years' studies in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, Copernicus presumably would also have learned some Italian. Professor Stefan Melkowski of <span class="ilh-all" data-foreign-title="Nicolaus Copernicus University in Toruń" data-lang-code="en" data-lang-name="英语" data-orig-title="Nicolaus Copernicus University in Toruń"><span class="ilh-page"><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nicolaus_Copernicus_University_in_Toru%C5%84&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nicolaus Copernicus University in Toruń（页面不存在）">Nicolaus Copernicus University in Toruń</a></span><span class="noprint ilh-comment">（<span class="ilh-lang">英语</span><span class="ilh-colon">：</span><span class="ilh-link"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicolaus_Copernicus_University_in_Toru%C5%84" title="en:Nicolaus Copernicus University in Toruń"><span dir="auto" lang="en">Nicolaus Copernicus University in Toruń</span></a></span>）</span></span> likewise asserts that Copernicus spoke both German and Polish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-O_historii_i_o_współczesności_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-O_historii_i_o_współczesności-26">[24]</a></sup></span>
</li>

</li>
<li id="cite_note-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-44">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">其中包括有关天文学家乔治·范·派尔巴赫（George von Peuerbach）的Theoricæ novæ planetarum，而且几乎可以肯定的是他还参加了Bernard of Biskupie 和 Wojciech Krypa of Szamotuły 的讲座，也许还参加了其他天文学学者的讲座，诸如Jan of Głogów、Michał of Wrocław (Breslau)、 Wojciech of Pniewy和Marcin Bylica of Olkusz等。</span>

</li>
<li id="cite_note-56"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-56">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">其名为 <i>Nicolai Copernici de hypothesibus motuum coelestium a se constitutis commentariolus</i> 也许是抄写者给出的题目</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-74"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-74">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Rosen <a href="#Reference-Rosen-1995">(1995, pp. 187–92)</a>, originally published in 1967 in <i>Saggi su Galileo Galilei </i>. Rosen is particularly scathing about this and other statements in <i>The Sleepwalkers</i>, which he criticizes as inaccurate.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-86"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-86">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Fantoli <a href="#Reference-Fantoli-2005">(2005, pp. 118–19)</a>; Finocchiaro <a href="#Reference-Finocchiaro-1989">(1989, pp. 148, 153)</a>. On-line copies of Finocchiaro's translations of the relevant documents, <a class="external text" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20070930013053/http://astro.wcupa.edu/mgagne/ess362/resources/finocchiaro.html#inqminutes" rel="nofollow">Inquisition Minutes of 25 February 1616</a> and <a class="external text" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20070930013053/http://astro.wcupa.edu/mgagne/ess362/resources/finocchiaro.html#certificate" rel="nofollow">Cardinal Bellarmine's certificate of 26 May 1616</a>, have been made available by Gagné <a href="#Reference-Gagne-2005">(2005)</a>. This notice of the decree would not have prevented Galileo from discussing heliocentrism solely as a mathematical hypothesis, but a stronger <a class="external text" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20070930013053/http://astro.wcupa.edu/mgagne/ess362/resources/finocchiaro.html#specinj" rel="nofollow">formal injunction</a> <a href="#Reference-Finocchiaro-1989">(Finocchiaro, 1989, p. 147-148)</a> not to teach it "in any way whatever, either orally or in writing", allegedly issued to him by the Commissary of the Holy Office, Father Michelangelo Segizzi, would certainly have done so <a href="#Reference-Fantoli-2005">(Fantoli, 2005, pp. 119–20, 137)</a>. There has been much controversy over whether the copy of this injunction in the Vatican archives is authentic; if so, whether it was ever issued; and if so, whether it was legally valid <a href="#Reference-Fantoli-2005">(Fantoli, 2005, pp. 120–43)</a>.</span>
</li>
</ol>

<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">

<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Linton (2004, pp.39, 119). Copernicus was not the first to propose a heliocentric system. A Greek mathematician and astronomer, Aristarchus of Samos, had done so as early as the third century BCE; but there is little evidence that Aristarchus developed his ideas beyond a very basic outline (Dreyer, 1953, pp. 135-48) 。哥白尼不是第一个创立日心说的人，希腊数学家、天文学家阿利斯塔克在公元前3世纪创立日心说，但是没有对其进行发展改进。</span>

<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Copernicus seems to have drawn up some notes on the displacement of good coin from circulation by debased coin while he was at Olsztyn in 1519. He made them the basis of a report on the matter, written in German, which he presented to the Prussian Diet held in 1522 at Grudziadz... He later drew up a revised and enlarged version of his little treatise, this time in Latin, and setting forth a general theory of money, for presentation to the Diet of 1528." Agngus Armitage, The World of Copernicus, 1951, p.91.</span>

<li id="cite_note-Moore5262-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Moore5262_15-0"><sup><b>14.0</b></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Moore5262_15-1"><sup><b>14.1</b></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">"[Watzenrode] was also firm, and the Teutonic Knights, who remained a constant menace, did not like him at all; the Grand Master of the order once described him as 'the devil incarnate'. <li id="cite_note-google19-30"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-google19_30-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Although great importance has frequently been ascribed to this fact, it does not imply that Copernicus considered himself to be a German. The 'nationes' of a medieval university had nothing in common with nations in the modern sense of the word. Students who were natives of Prussia and Silesia were automatically described as belonging to the Natio Germanorum. Furthmore, at Bologna, this was the 'privileged' nation; consequently, Copernicus had very good reason for inscribing himself on its register." Koyre, p. 21</span>

Johnson, p. 23.</span>
